Spring and Autumn

Wet Faction and Wine Barrel

— Zhan Lu

The Prohibition Law, which was suspended after being approved by three-quarters of the forty-eight states in the United States, has been satisfied for more than thirteen years from its promulgation in 1920 until the day Roosevelt took office this year in March.

The Americans who advocate prohibition are the Drys, and those who oppose prohibition are the Wets. There are more Drys in the Republican Party and more Wets in the Democratic Party. In mid-November last year, Roosevelt was elected President, and the Wet faction of the Democratic Party rose. This newspaper reported that in the recent bizarre entourage of Mr. Luo's inauguration, there was a wine shop dragging a wine barrel, which was a grand demonstration by the Wet faction. With Roosevelt, who relaxes the ban on alcohol, as the head of state, the general foreign-style, Liu Ling and Li Taibai, should applaud the marching wine barrel and shout their slogans wildly.

I think it would be best to have articles praising the three-day wine journey written on the flags in front of the wine barrel, so that it can further promote the Wet faction. Bai Xiangshan of our country is a giant in the Wet faction. He has a poem praising wine that is even better than Liu Ling's Ode to the Virtue of Wine. I will write it down below. If someone translates it into a foreign poem and presents it to the Wet faction comrades in the New World, it would be an excellent gift.

The wine in the cup is full and clear, and it does not boast of its own merits; If I don't boast, people won't know, so I will speak for it now: When a good general faces a great enemy, he leads thousands of soldiers; They drink a single cup into the river, and their hearts are as one in facing death. A strong man grinds his seven heads, and his courage and anger roar; A single drunk forgets his revenge, and his four limbs are as boneless. When Donghai killed the filial wife, the sky changed early and lasted for months; A single sip stopped the drought, and the rain did not stop all night. The atmosphere of the Qin prison in Xianyang, the grievances and pains were condensed into matter; It refuses to dissipate for thousands of years, but a single watering also dissipates it. Moreover, the hatred of children, and the sorrow and pain of the secluded; A quick drink will eliminate everything, like frost receiving the spring sun, Only then do I know that wine is the most spiritual, and nothing can compare to it.

The power of wine, the authority of wine, whether in the Old World or the New World, cannot be ignored for a lifetime.

Important People and Celebrities

— Juan Yun

丨My Fantasy丨

The busy legs of newspaper reporters [running around and interviewing] allow us to often read profound theories and brilliant insights in the newspaper. Naturally, the actions of important people and celebrities can be used as news material. Important people and celebrities are the pillars of society.

But important people and celebrities are divided into two types. In the country, there are important people who preside over national affairs, in the city government there are important people who preside over municipal affairs, and in business there are also important people in the business world. Perhaps I think that Lao Wang, who drives the streetcar, is also an important person, because his family of seven depends on him driving the car to make a living.

It's just that he is considered an important person in his own family, but he is not necessarily considered an important person in other people's eyes. Someone who is considered an important person in China is not necessarily considered an important person in the eyes of foreigners. Or, he was considered an important person before, but after losing power or dying, he can no longer be considered an important person.

Therefore, the title of "important person" is only applicable during the period of power.

Celebrities seem to be different. Whether in the past, present, or future, we always admire them and respectfully call them XX celebrities.

There are many, many celebrities. Those who write novels are called famous novelists, those who write poems are called famous great poets. Whether studying philosophy, science, politics, law, economics, or medicine, they can be admired everywhere. There are several reputable celebrities in the entire world, and as small as a county or town. I have always had a strange dream in my life, dreaming that I will also become a celebrity.

Last month, I saw a special dispatch about Xiao Bonai visiting the Temple of Heaven in Beiping. I can very much recall that I have visited the Temple of Heaven three times. It really makes me admire him, because Xiao Bonai is a celebrity, especially a world celebrity. There are quite a few celebrities in Shanghai who have already done many great and amazing things. What others often say and what is published in the newspapers, whether it is the directors of various banks, the founders of companies, saving the country and raising relief funds, municipal affairs, and the business community, it seems that among so many people in Shanghai, only a few Shanghai celebrities are enthusiastic! I often think that if I could be lucky enough to become a Shanghai celebrity, it would naturally be very difficult. Dreams cannot become reality, and I was born with a pitiful skeleton! At least I cannot cope with these versatile and great various undertakings, but I always fantasize like this, maybe I will become a celebrity.

Pig

— Yong Zi

丨Useless Myself丨

There are some beggars in Shanghai who specialize in following people, stepping in their footsteps and shaking a paper funnel to ask for money. This kind of begging is called pig driving. They treat the benefactors as pigs. There is a kind of bandit in Shanghai who specializes in hiding in remote and dark places, waiting for a single man to walk by lonely and cool. The bandits shout, raise their guns, and rush forward to strip the single man's clothes. This kind of robbery is called pig killing, and they also treat the robbed person as a pig. Giving money to beggars and giving clothes to bandits, but in the end, he got the title of pig, in this age of declining morals, a good person really can't do it.

Some people say that China is a sleeping pig. Oh my! I dare not, dare not. One agreement, one condition, nibble on this piece, dig on that piece. Our China is a country with great capacity for generosity, doing some good deeds, and not caring at all. You love to pick up what, just pick up what, ask for it, what, strangely pathetic. Oh, no, like this mother-in-law, he drove the pig. This is not okay, a good person can't do it. Oh, it's even more wrong, not giving alms, the beggar becomes a bandit, a shout, the gun pointed at the head, if you don't obey, he will pull the trigger, if you obey, he will strip your clothes, and carry out pig killing. It's very pitiful, China is always in a position of being driven and killed, where does this come from?

Being driven by beggars is annoying, but you can call the patrol to catch them. But when the patrol comes, the beggars leave, and you can't do anything about it. Being stripped of clothes by bandits, you can report the arrest, but by the time the patrol arrives, the bandits have gone far away. It is said that this kind of patrol who is willing to follow you to catch beggars and thieves, releasing a horse after the fact, is considered good. Some irresponsible patrols, you go and tell him with all your sweat, but he smiles indifferently and says, Pig, why don't you catch the beggar or robber? Now they have run away, why are you so anxious?

Alas, pig, useless myself, what's good to say!

Dragon Lantern and Puyi

— Zhang Zhihen

丨Is it One or Two?丨

Puyi, what did I think you were? Originally, it was a dragon lantern that was being manipulated by people. Why do I say this? Listen to me!

A few days ago, dragon lanterns were set off in Taicang City, and the scene was unprecedentedly grand. I lived in the most lively central area, sat by the window on the floor, and looked out into the distance, feasting my eyes. After dusk, people from all over the city gathered enthusiastically on both sides of the street, waiting for the arrival of these dragon lanterns competing for beauty and splendor. Soon, one or two firecrackers broke the silence in the distance, followed by loud cheers from the crowd, saying: [The dragon lantern is here, the dragon lantern is here,] Sure enough, the music team walked slowly, noisily beating ancient Chinese gongs and drums. In an instant, the lights were all lit up, and several lifelike dragon lanterns were already in front of us. Suddenly, there were firecrackers that shook the roof tiles, vibrating our eardrums. The dragon lantern danced, twisting and turning into the sky. Inside the dragon's body, there were lights of various colors, and the two dragon eyes were made of dry electricity, and the light flickered, dazzling people's eyes. Looking at the dancing posture of those dragon lanterns from a distance, who wouldn't say they are just like real dragons? But looking closely, the abdomen of the dragon lantern is supported by a dozen short bamboo sticks, and a dozen people each hold a stick, manipulating these almost lifelike dragon lanterns. Ah! Dragon lantern, dragon lantern! I thought you were dancing freely, who knew you were being held and moved by people?

Puyi, who is called the executive in the Northeast, is said to want to call himself solitary and widowed. In his own opinion, it is not that he is taking advantage of the time to [rise like a dragon]; even among the group of [followers], they also regard him as the true son of heaven with [dragon patterns and phoenix posture], but in the eyes of others, what is the difference between this Puyi executive and the dragon lantern manipulated by others? Look! Those many dwarves are pulling him along!

Puyi, ah! What did I think you were? Originally, it was a dragon lantern that was being manipulated by people.

Long novel

Northeast Fourth Company Commander

— Zhang Genshui

In the first episode, Zhao Ziqiang said cordially, pushing the food: Old lady, don't worry, although I am a soldier, I don't take advantage of others. As the saying goes: Good iron is not used to make nails, and good people don't become soldiers. I don't agree with this sentence. Soldiers work for the country, how much money do they get? They eat mixed noodle nests and wear ragged clothes, but they are all doing things that sell their lives. Of course, there are also bad brothers, but it's not that people become bad as soon as they become soldiers, nor is it that good people don't become soldiers. It's just because the people who recruit soldiers don't recruit good people to be soldiers at all. Besides, being a soldier is really hard. Generally, as long as people can cope with it, they won't become soldiers. Look, I am a soldier, but I am a little different from other soldiers. As he spoke, he walked straight into the courtyard. Jiang also felt that this person spoke very frankly and accompanied him, walking all the way to the courtyard. The courtyard is three north rooms and two east-west厢 rooms. An upper person, with a servant, is living a good life here. Zhao Ziqiang looked through all the rooms inside and out, and then said to Jiang: I know that your family has a simple population, and there is no one in my family. Our old master is very old-fashioned, please rest assured. Jiang said: What are we worried about, living with people like you, what's wrong with that? Zhao Ziqiang laughed: To be honest, people always think that good people don't become soldiers, so they are not happy to be with anyone. Even if you say you are renting a house, the landlord is afraid that you won't pay the rent. Jiang laughed: You are joking. Zhao Ziqiang said seriously: I am telling the truth. Even renting this house: I also asked several people to talk to the landlord, to make sure there was nothing wrong, and paid three months' rent in advance, and then I rented it. In short, we soldiers are always looked down upon. After speaking, he sighed, and then said: I always hope that we soldiers can win back this tone. As he spoke, he came out again. Jiang felt that this person spoke very frankly, and there was a bit of joy in his heart, so she quickly said: Company commander, sit down in our house, would you like to have a cup of tea first? Zhao Ziqiang stood and thought for a while, and laughed: Okay, I should also go to your house to pay my respects. So Jiang led the way in front, opened the wind door, and let him in. (8)

Shanghai Night Talk

Strolling Under the Neon Lights

— Zhang Ruogu

Neon lights flash everywhere with horizontal Chinese characters, vertical Roman letters CAFE, and Arabic numerals 1234. The show at the Paris Grand Theater ended at half past five. From the store selling phonographs, the sound of [The Melody of a Virgin's Heart] is broadcast using a loudspeaker. The short needle of the Mito Night Light Standard clock points to the VII character. I hear in my ear: [The Big Evening News…Extra Edition of the Old Shen Bao]. In front of me is the window display of a cosmetics store: powder, perfume, lipstick, and KOTEX are displayed together.

A siren sounds, and the blood-red light turns yellow. Trams, cars, rickshaws, and fish move forward. Cars, cars, people, people, people, trams, trams, people, people, people, rickshaws, rickshaws, people, people, people, trams, cars, rickshaws, people, people, people.

In the glass window of the Geneva watch shop, the platinum watch emits dazzling brilliance, and the long and short hands are quietly frozen on the white porcelain dial. In the large glass frame of a certain lady's photo studio, portraits of urban men and women are pasted: a white-haired Western girl, a broad-nosed Shanghai lady, a soldier with a chest full of medals, a naked Western baby, and a foreign old lady wearing fashionable new clothes and a wig.

The seasonal fruits in the glass window of the grocery store, red apples, green lettuce, green olive oil sardines, scarlet blood oranges, and golden Guangdong bananas, are brightly colored, tempting the appetites of white Russian vagrants on the sidewalk.

The window display of the candy and bread shop is like opening a painting exhibition, displaying gorgeously decorated candy boxes. Each box is a bright picture, Swiss snow scenery, a naked jade-skinned seductive woman wearing light gauze, a lucky black cat, a French Louis dynasty lady wearing a large pleated skirt and holding a small parasol, and a Hollywood romantic movie star. Next to the Santa Claus idol in a white beard and red robe, there is a chocolate Chinese pagoda.

Bright electric light signs are hung one after another at the entrance of the alley: Turkey, Khitan, Paris, Harbin, Greater Shanghai, and geographical place names are used up. There are also palace, Xuan palace, ... palace-like names, but narrow massage parlors like pigeon lofts.

At the crossroads, on the left and right are car parks: French Citroen, Renault; Italian Fiat; American Nash. Behind a Ford car is a special large car for the foreign embassy.

[Jehol lost...Tang Yulin fled...Zhang Xueliang is anxious...He Yingqin arrives in Beijing...Antiques moved to Shanghai...Great earthquake in the East...Chiang Kai-shek arrives in Baoding...] The boys selling evening newspapers and the old guns with smoky faces are rushing and shouting.

The patrol calmly blows the whistle, turning on the street lights: trams, cars, rickshaws, people, people, people, rickshaws, trams, cars, people, people, people.

Education News

Headline News

Students in Various Schools in Hubei Province Prepare to Suspend Classes and March

(Hankou, 10th) Students from various schools throughout the province, in response to the fall of Jehol, will suspend classes and march. On the 9th, the school authorities asked the Provincial Party Department and the Education Department for instructions.

Education Circles in Anhui Province Purchase Aircraft

Donated 130,000 yuan, named Anhui Education No. On the 3rd of this month, the education circles in Anhui decided at a meeting to voluntarily raise 130,000 yuan from the education circles throughout the province to purchase an aircraft, named Anhui Education No. The fundraising method is to collect separately according to the administrative system, and the estimated amount is as follows: 1. 180,000 students from public and private elementary schools in the province, each saving half a copper coin a day, can save 20 cents in four months, totaling 36,000 yuan. 2. 6,000 students from provincial elementary schools, each saving one yuan a day, can save 80 cents in four months, totaling 4,800 yuan. 3. 12,000 students from public and private middle schools, each saving one yuan of food expenses a month, can save four yuan in four months, totaling 48,000 yuan. 4. 500 students from provincial universities, each saving two yuan of food and pocket money a month, can save eight yuan in four months, totaling 4,000 yuan. 5. 900 staff members and teachers of provincial educational institutions, each drawing three yuan a month, can draw eighteen yuan in six months, totaling 16,200 yuan. 6. Provincial elementary school teachers and staff each drawing one yuan a month, 500 people, totaling 3,000 yuan in six months. 7. 500 teachers and staff of county-run private secondary schools, each drawing two yuan a month, can get twelve yuan in six months, totaling 6,000 yuan. 8. 11,000 teachers and staff of county-run private elementary schools in various counties, each drawing 30 cents a month, can get 1.8 yuan each in six months, totaling 16,500 yuan. 9. 40 teachers and staff of provincial universities, each drawing eight yuan a month, can get 48 yuan each in six months, totaling 1,920 yuan. 10. Educational administrative personnel in 60 counties in various counties, each county drawing five yuan a month, can get 30 yuan each in six months, totaling 1,800 yuan, for a total of 138,220 yuan.

Beijing Middle Schools Request Improvement of Entrance Examination Methods

(Nanjing, 10th) The principals of middle schools in Beijing submitted a request to the Ministry of Education on the 10th to improve the entrance examination methods. (1) The entrance examination should respect the administrative power of the schools at the same time, that is, the schools should have the power to handle graduation. (2) The entrance examination should give special awards to passing students. (3) The standards of the entrance examination should strive for uniformity. (4) The entrance examination methods should strive for caution.

Representatives of Beijing-Tianjin Education Federation Visit He Yingqin

Transferring Elite Troops from Various Provinces to Recover Lost Territory

General Association of Teachers and Staff of National Universities Established in Beiping

(Special Dispatch from Beiping) Liu Shichuan and Song Jie, representatives of the Joint Association of Teachers and Staff of National Universities in Beijing and Tianjin, visited He Yingqin, Minister of Military and Political Affairs, at Jurentang, Zhonghai, at 10:00 am on the 8th. They requested that elite troops from various provinces be transferred north to join the troops stationed at the Yuguan Pass and along the Great Wall to recover Jehol and the lost territory of the Northeast on a specific date. They did not know He Yingqin's whereabouts in advance, so the two representatives, Liu and Song, still went to Jurentang, but returned without meeting him. According to the guard's words to the representatives, Minister He had already left for Baoding by car on the evening of the 7th to welcome Chairman Chiang. So the two representatives, Liu and Song, left a letter and left. The original letter is recorded below. Dear Sir, The fall of Jehol has endangered North China, and the people of the country share the debt, causing laughter from all nations. In addition to having telegraphed the government to severely punish the generals who lost the territory and implement emergency measures in wartime, the association has appointed representatives Song Jie and Liu Shichuan to visit you, requesting that elite troops from various provinces be transferred north to join the troops stationed at the Yuguan Pass and along the Great Wall to recover Jehol and the lost territory of the Northeast on a specific date, in order to wash away the national shame. Please grant us an audience. We are looking forward to it. Sincerely, He, Minister of Military and Political Affairs, from the Joint Association of Teachers and Staff of National Universities in Beijing and Tianjin.

Liu Shi-chuan's Interview

A reporter specially interviewed Liu Shi-chuan, a representative of the Beiping-Tianjin Teachers' Association, to inquire about the association's purpose in visiting He Yingqin and the situation of organizing the National Federation of Teachers and Staff for Resistance Against Japan. According to his reply, as follows: Our association held an emergency meeting of the standing committee and decided to send representatives to visit the minister. However, Minister He had gone to Baoding to welcome Chairman Chiang Kai-shek, so he was not able to meet with him. After Minister He returns to Beiping, we will visit him again. There are two purposes for the visit: (1) Please immediately dispatch elite troops from various provinces north to join the garrison troops at Yuguan and along the Great Wall to recover Rehe and the lost territories of the Northeast within a limited time to avenge the national humiliation. (2) Inquire about the central government's preparations for resisting Japan. As for the Beiping-Tianjin Teachers' Association initiating the organization of the National Federation of Teachers and Staff for Resistance Against Japan, Mr. Mou Mo, the liaison representative for the third district, has been in contact in Beijing, Shanghai, Hangzhou and other places, and has reportedly made considerable progress. Mr. Jia Cheng-zhang, the liaison representative for the fourth district, has arrived in Guangzhou to contact and organize the National Federation of Teachers and Staff for Resistance Against Japan. The general association will be located in Beiping, with branch associations in various provinces and important commercial ports such as Shanghai, Hankou, and Tianjin. Its purpose is to take the recovery of Rehe and the lost territories of the Northeast as the standard. Teachers and staff nationwide should lead the people of the whole country, vowing to resist Japan with one heart and one mind, he said.

Yanjing University

The Yanjing University Chinese Teachers and Staff Anti-Japanese Association held a meeting in the Saint Building on the 8th and decided to send a telegram to the National Government requesting punishment for Tang [Yulin], and to request Chiang Kai-shek to quickly go north to supervise the army. The original telegram is recorded below: To the National Government: The national territory of Rehe has fallen into enemy hands again, and the overall situation is deteriorating to this extreme. One mistake after another, how can North China be used as resources for a strong enemy? We hope the government will strictly enforce military discipline, and those who desert their posts, such as Tang Yulin, should be sentenced to death. We especially hope that Chairman Chiang will go north to supervise the army immediately, internally to restore the morale of the people, and externally to maintain international dignity. When international trust and popular support are gained, then the government can survive. This is an unchanging truth. Respectfully, the Yanjing University Chinese Teachers and Staff Anti-Japanese Association of Beiping.

The Process of the European Education Survey Group's Investigation (1)

Investigation Work in Europe

Q: How was the investigation work in Europe conducted? A: The League of Nations' investigation of China's education was conducted by the International Institute of Intellectual Co-operation of the League of Nations. Although the Chinese European Education Survey Group was dispatched by the Chinese government, its work in Europe mostly cooperated with the International Institute of Intellectual Co-operation, as China is a member of the institute. The institute's duties are also to promote international cultural communication, exchange, and mutual assistance. The education survey group set sail from Shanghai on August 5th, heading directly to Italy. At the end of August, they arrived in Geneva and met with the institute's staff and Dr. Rajchman, the director of the League of Nations Health Organization, who has always expressed sympathy for China. Before our group arrived in Europe, they had already planned the countries to be investigated, the investigation schedule, and the matters that should be cooperated with each country, and obtained the assistance of various countries. The original plan stipulated an investigation period of four months, the first three months in Poland, Germany, and France, and the last month in the United Kingdom (but the United Kingdom was not yet fully confirmed at that time). The plan set by the institute was indeed very thoughtful. However, the members of our group believed that the education systems of various European countries each had their own strengths, and if we could not observe the education of all important countries, it would be difficult to fulfill the government's original intention in dispatching us. Therefore, we discussed with the institute about adding Italy, Denmark, Austria, and Soviet Russia, and asked the institute to seek the consent of these countries. At the same time, we submitted a request to the Ministry of Education in our country to extend the investigation period by two months, for a total of six months. Later, we were fortunate to succeed in both aspects. Once the plan was finalized, our group left Geneva for Poland on September 1st and arrived on September 3rd. On the same day, Dr. Huaszek, Director of Supervision Rauboziński, and Dr. Qu Heng, representing the Polish Ministry of Education, discussed with our group the pre-prepared visit plan. After careful discussion, we generally considered it appropriate and began the investigation on September 6th. In addition to visiting Warsaw, the capital of Poland, for several days, we also visited Bygdoszcz, Gdynia, Krakow, Katowice, Chorzów, and several villages in the remaining twenty days. Generally speaking, we have gained a rough understanding of the education in western, southern, and northwestern Poland. On October 1st, we transferred to Berlin and discussed the schedule for the investigation in Germany with representatives from Berkell, Hecker, Liddman, the German Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and the Prussian Ministry of Education. October 5th to 10th was the school holiday period in Germany. Our group took advantage of this leisure period to go to Denmark for investigation. We arrived in Copenhagen on the same day, and the next day we discussed the schedule with the Danish Ministry of Education. The ministry sent Dr. Jensen to accompany us to visit various places every day. For a total of one week, we gained a rough understanding of urban and rural education. Then, according to the determined schedule, we returned to Lübeck in Germany on October 11th. Dr. Hecker came to greet us and immediately acted as our translator. Our group then went from Lübeck to Hamburg, then to Düsseldorf, then to Cologne, then to Essen, then to Stuttgart, then to Frankfurt, then to Munich, and then to Dresden, visiting dozens of cities and countless villages before returning to Berlin. This was because Germany's educational achievements have long been famous in the world, and Germany does not have a unified school system, with each state governing itself and having its own strengths, so we had to spend more time and energy. The day after completing the investigation in Germany, we rushed to France. We met with Professor Langevin, Dr. Barriere, a representative of the Ministry of Education, the Dean of the Faculty of Science of the University of Paris, and other famous figures in the education field, and discussed the schedule for the investigation in France. The investigation period was one month, divided into visits to the four university districts of Paris, Nancy, Lyon, and Strasbourg, and their rural areas, with each place ranging from two or three days to more than ten days. After completing the investigation in France, our group went to the United Kingdom. In London, Dr. Ball, an employee of the British International Institute of Intellectual Co-operation, Dr. Wood, a representative of the Ministry of Education, and others took care of everything. For the first few days, we mostly held meetings with the Ministry of Education and famous figures in the education field to discuss the system and ideological issues of British education. Then we went to Oxford University, Cambridge University, Reading University, Leeds and other places, investigating each place for several days before returning to London to investigate the education of the City of London until the end of December, when we finally concluded. Our group had to leave the United Kingdom and go to Italy again, as the investigation schedule in Italy started on January 5th. On January 5th, our colleagues arrived in Geneva, Italy. Professor Pompianri, a representative of the Italian government, came to greet us. The next day, we began the investigation there. We spent only one day before going to Milan for three days, then to Rome, from Rome to Naples, then to Pompeii, and then back to Rome before going to Florence, then to Bologna, and then to Venice. The investigation in Italy ended here. On January 21st, we arrived in Vienna, the capital of Austria. We spent several days discussing Austrian education in the Ministry of Education, the Municipal Education Bureau, and other places. Afterwards, for more than a week, we devoted ourselves to visiting various schools and educational institutions, both in cities and villages, taking care of both sides. On February 3rd, we left Austria and entered Russia, arriving in Moscow on the 5th. Employees of the Chinese-Soviet Conference Delegation in our country and representatives of the Soviet Russian government came to take care of everything. That afternoon, we discussed the visit procedure and began the next day, completing it in ten days. The European investigation work of our group came to an end here. This is a rough outline of the investigation trips to various places. As for the content of the investigation, it was very extensive, from kindergartens to universities, from the central education administration to the education administration of the smallest local units, from classroom teaching to film education and sound education, we stopped at each one. Therefore, the investigation schedule was particularly busy. We started visiting at eight or nine o'clock in the morning and did not finish until six or seven o'clock in the afternoon. The only time for organizing notes was at night. However, the governments of various countries often took advantage of this time to invite us to the national theater to watch plays, and on Sundays, we often went to the countryside to visit teachers' sanatoriums, local education conferences, student field trips, and other activities related to education. Therefore, in these few months, all the members of our group felt that time was not enough, and foreign friends were all worried that our group's working hours were too long. However, we ourselves felt that as weak individuals, we were responsible for this important task of investigation, and we had to make up for our shortcomings with diligence (to be continued).

Highly Treated in Europe

Q: How was the reception in various countries? A: Before our group set off, the International Institute of Intellectual Co-operation of the League of Nations had already contacted the governments of the countries concerned, so all countries were prepared in advance, and therefore the reception was extremely considerate. Whenever we arrived in a country, government representatives would personally come to the station to pick us up. For example, the Vice Minister of Education and the Director of the Department of Foreign Affairs came to the station to welcome us. When we arrived in Italy, the Italian government specially sent the Vice Minister of Education to Milan to welcome us. When we arrived in Germany, in addition to government representatives, former Minister of Education Dr. Berkell also came to the station in person. The situation in France was also roughly the same. All countries invited us in the name of the government. Whenever we arrived in a city, the mayor, the director of the Municipal Education Bureau, either came to greet us in person or sent people to receive us, all doing their best to show the hospitality of the host, inviting us to meals, watching plays, or specially holding concerts, which became a common practice everywhere. Whenever we arrived at a school, the principals and teachers were extremely happy, inviting us to stay for meals, sign our names, send student grades, and take commemorative photos, which was almost the case everywhere. The governments of various countries, as well as various schools and educational institutions, provided as much educational material as possible, which was of great help to our colleagues' reference. This was because this was the first time that the Chinese government had officially dispatched an education survey group, and the governments and schools of various countries were willing to cooperate with the Chinese education community, which represented the high-level culture and history of the East, in order to communicate Chinese and Western cultures and promote the progress of mankind. Under this noble mentality of the governments and education communities of various countries, our colleagues were treated favorably everywhere.

Handling of Materials

Q: What is the nature of the reference materials obtained, and how will they be handled? A: The materials obtained this time are very numerous. Most of them were donated by the governments and educational institutions of various countries, and a small part were purchased by our group. All of them were packed in wooden boxes and sent back after the investigation of each country was completed. Each country had at least one large box, and some had as many as three or four wooden boxes. The nature of the materials is: (1) education laws and regulations, (2) education books and newspapers, (3) student grades, (4) other items related to education. These materials can be of great reference value to the education community. While we were in Europe, we discussed the handling of these materials and planned to organize an exhibition or display them in the library of the Ministry of Education after they were sorted out, so that people in the education community could easily refer to them. How to handle them in the future will naturally have to be decided by the Ministry of Education.

Advantages of European Education

Q: What are your impressions of European education? A: Our group will definitely publish an investigation report in the future. The situation of European education and its contributions to the construction of Chinese education will be described in detail in the report. At this time, the investigation has just ended, and we have not yet been able to sort it out. Without the resolution of the group as a whole, it is difficult to express formal opinions. However, after several months of investigation, I have many personal observations, so I might as well tell you some of the important ones from my personal perspective.

Education is Increasingly Valued

(1) European countries recognize the importance of education more keenly than before, and unanimously regard education as the most fundamental and most effective tool for improving individuals, society, and the country. Therefore, individuals, society, and the country are also unanimously striving to engage in education. The financial difficulties of individuals and countries in various countries are more severe than before the war. However, the number of students in schools at all levels is higher than before, and the amount of education funding undertaken by governments at all levels is also higher than before. The construction and equipment of schools are better than before. All of this is sufficient to prove that various countries recognize education and strive for education.

Efforts in Universal Education

(2) The emphasis on universal education. In the past, we have heard people say that European education is class education, and the poor and lowly classes cannot enjoy it, the reasons being (1) high tuition fees, (2) complex school system. In fact, European countries are currently paying attention to the education of all people. Compulsory education not only has no tuition fees, but also provides school supplies. Many countries not only provide good kindergartens for young children, but also provide meals and clothing without any fees. Kindergarten education in Europe is a relief business for poor families. As for education above elementary school, those belonging to vocational crafts are charged very low fees, and poor children can easily enter school. Other restrictions are not strict. Those belonging to ordinary secondary schools have higher tuition fees and very strict selection, but the government has set up free places. All poor but intelligent and hardworking children do not have to worry about not being able to enter school. There are also some popular education institutions in society that are sufficient to increase the knowledge and skills of the general public. Those who are determined to study can make good use of them. Therefore, in reality, everyone has the opportunity to study. As for the school systems of European countries, they are indeed complex, but the difficulty of mutual conversion between schools is not as great as it was once rumored. Therefore, European education is also the education of all people.

Extremely Good Academic Atmosphere

Third, the academic atmosphere is good. In any country in Europe, from middle school to university, we have not heard of students causing disturbances, we have not heard of students making suggestions and forcing schools to adopt them, we have not heard of students disobeying school orders, and there is absolutely no such thing as self-selecting principals or expelling education. Even in the Soviet Union, there is absolutely no such fact. The student self-government association in Soviet secondary schools has strong guidance from school teachers, and students must obey. Generally speaking, Europeans believe that autonomy and obedience are indeed essential elements for building a sound country and society. Students must receive this kind of training at school before they can become good citizens. As for the supervision of school education, the responsibility lies with the government, and the government's supervision lies with the parliament and the citizens. Young students are not allowed to abandon their studies and overstep their authority. Because of the good academic atmosphere in various schools, students can study with peace of mind and achieve good results. The education industry is not only on the right track, but has never been derailed.

Strict Screening of Teachers

Fourth, the teachers are excellent. Teachers in primary and secondary schools in European countries generally have longer training periods than in China, and they are very serious, and they have to pass strict examinations before they can enter school and graduate. After graduation, they must go through a considerable period of internship before they can become formal teachers, so their teachers are indeed better than those in China. Once formally appointed, they are in permanent service. Any principal or head of education cannot easily dismiss them unless there are special and serious faults. The salary of teachers, whether in middle school or elementary school, is sufficient for the use of a family, so they can work with peace of mind because they have no worries about their family. We often see teachers in primary and secondary schools who have served in a school for thirty years with gray hair and old age. This is the reason.

Emphasis on Practical Education

Fifth, emphasis on practical science and physical education. In the past, we have also heard that European education is too biased towards culture, with too much Latin and Greek in middle schools and too little applied science. This view is also only knowing one thing. European elementary schools are the basic education for life, and naturally take the knowledge and skills necessary for life as the main thing. Above middle school, there are two types of schools, one is ordinary middle schools, which mainly prepare for university, and the other is vocational schools such as agriculture, industry, commerce, home economics, and politics. These schools completely focus on applied sciences. The curriculum of ordinary middle schools still retains Latin and Greek, and some have abandoned them. Even in the United Kingdom, which pays attention to Latin and Greek public middle schools, they now also pay attention to handicraft (woodworking and metalworking) and science. In Russia, the trend of focusing on science and handicraft is greater than in any other country. Latin and Greek are no longer seen in the curriculum. Any student has to enter the metalworking and woodworking shops, and those who cannot work are not allowed to be students. Because Soviet Russia is striving to complete its industrialization within ten years, and the citizens it needs are citizens who can work, its education has to pay special attention to applied science and handicraft. The handicraft achievements of other countries are admirable. Senior elementary schools and middle schools all have metalworking and woodworking shops, and the equipment of their shops is almost the same as that of formally trained workers. Therefore, the students' achievements are very good, and they can manufacture the instruments and specimens used in scientific teaching themselves. According to the explanations of the school authorities, the country is currently facing economic difficulties, and the school funds are insufficient, so they cannot purchase various instruments as they used to, and they have no choice but to train students to manufacture them themselves, which costs only 20-30% of the purchase price.

Promote Military Training

In addition, all schools pay more attention to physical education than before the war, and their exercises are very different from the soft exercises we practice in our country. Even sports such as basketball, football, and baseball, which cost a little more, are not commonly used by various schools. The most widely promoted ones are various games of rural children in our country, as well as the methods of running, kneeling, crawling, and walking. Swimming is highly valued. Long-distance outdoor travel is also vigorously promoted in Germany and Poland. This kind of physical education method is more practical, cost-effective, and effective. The emphasis on science, handicraft, and physical education not only has profound significance in education, but also has important relations in social life and national defense. Therefore, in later social life, there is a trend that those who cannot work cannot live. Applied science is more closely related to general life than other academic disciplines, so education has to attach importance to it. Moreover, the undercurrents in the world today are more severe than before the war. All countries not only pay attention to military preparations, but also to the preparation of soldiers. The physical education that is currently popular is actually the most effective military training. Handicraft is also an essential skill for soldiers, because soldiers must not only be able to use weapons, but also be able to build fortifications and make the simplest repairs to military equipment. School education, social life, and national defense must be linked together, which is an urgent task for China. I hope the government and compatriots will pay close attention to it.

Report Will Be Drafted Soon

The above is just a simple explanation of the most important points. After all the members of our group return to China, we will immediately start drafting the report and ask the people of the country to correct us. The abilities of our colleagues are weak, the scope of education is too broad, and the time is too short, so the results obtained may not only fail to satisfy the hopes of the government and the people of the country, but also fail to satisfy the wishes of our colleagues themselves. However, our group has established considerable relationships and deep feelings with the governments and education communities of the countries we have visited. If we can continue to contact them, the benefits to each other will naturally be many. We especially hope that in the future, experts will continue to go to various countries to conduct more detailed and specialized investigations, and the colleagues of our group will do their best to fulfill the responsibility of liaison and introduction, so the results will be even more significant (End).

Philco Radio's Rapid Business Growth

Philco Radio Corporation was established not long ago, but its business is thriving, and few can compare with it. In 1928, the radio industry in the United States was already very developed, with numerous factories everywhere, many of which already enjoyed great fame. Philco Radio Corporation was established in this year of the most intense competition in the industry. That year, the United States produced a total of four million radios, worth 700 million gold dollars, and Philco Radio sold 100,000 units, worth about 7.5 million gold dollars, accounting for about 2.5% of the national business.

In 1929, Philco Radio Corporation was the first to invent the automatic volume control and improved its sales methods, so it was able to sell 500,000 units out of the total national sales of five million units, accounting for about 10% of the national business.

In 1930, the third year after the founding of Philco Radio Corporation, the national output was four million units, each worth 125 yuan, totaling 500 million gold dollars. Philco sold 800,000 units, accounting for almost one-fifth of the national radio business.

In 1931, the American business market was sluggish, and many factories closed down, but Philco's output increased to one million units, worth 86 million gold dollars, accounting for one-third of the US industry. In the second half of the year, it accounted for 40% of the industry. Last year, the company's business was even more prosperous, expanding its capital and adding equipment. It is said that it can now produce 12,500 radios per day. Now, it is also engaged in the improvement of television technology (i.e., video receivers) and other radio-related inventions, striving for perfection.

The company has a branch in China, with offices and showrooms at 96 Nanjing Road, Shanghai, telephone number 17930. All are welcome to visit and listen. (The company also manages Philco brand batteries, etc.)

Features of the Latest Style Stewart 106 Radio

— Zhenzhi

The Stewart 106 radio has six features:

(1) Suppression of noise between stations.

(2) [Q] Circuit.

(3) Delayed automatic volume control.

(4) Using the latest type 59 power vacuum tube to reduce humming and increase power to 2/10ths of the PZ pentode vacuum tube.

(5) Expanding the harmonic range to enable reception of the latest frequency of 540 kilocycles.

(6) Equipped with the latest powerful power transformer to prevent any possibility of burnout.

The above three features (1), (2), and (3) are important for the reception of any radio, so these features are bound to become the standard of the radio industry in the future. All radio enthusiasts need to understand the role of these features. This will not only enable you to master this new radio and get satisfactory results, but also give you the basic knowledge to choose a good radio. These features are described below:

Noise Suppression Between Stations

One of the shortcomings of automatic volume control is that noise often occurs when tuning between two stations. This shortcoming is corrected in the 106 model by the presence of inter-station noise suppression and Q circuit.

The fundamental principle of inter-station noise suppression is to limit man-made or atmospheric noise between two stations. Please note the meaning of [between two stations]. There is currently no radio circuit that can isolate noise and audio signals that have been received by the antenna. So when you talk about noise suppression between two stations, please do not forget this fact.

The effect of inter-station noise suppression can be explained as follows. Suppose there are many broadcast stations in the air, and the sound of the signals they emit has various intensities for a certain area. If you draw many vertical lines with their heights representing the intensity of each incoming signal, you get the shape shown in Figure 1. ABCDEF are six

stations, each station has different signal strength. When the listener turns the tuning dial, these signals are successively tuned in. Suppose that at this particular time, the atmospheric noise in the air can be represented by a straight line at the height of station C. This means that the atmospheric noise entering at this time has the same loudness as the audio signal emitted by station C. Because atmospheric noise exists uniformly at all points on the tuning dial, we can naturally use a horizontal line H with a height of C to represent it. The programs transmitted from stations ABDF are often mixed with atmospheric noise equal to H. However, this noise is extremely small compared to the total volume of stations ABDF, so it can be masked by them. However, listening to the sounds of stations AB can receive a lot of noise. In addition, there is an extremely difficult problem to solve, that is, when the radio is tuned between stations CE, its automatic volume control automatically raises the machine's selectivity to the highest level, and then all the atmospheric noise is brought in until station B is reached. This noise is extremely unpleasant when tuning.

If we give this radio a variable selectivity control, we can reduce its maximum selectivity to a certain value, set it to the horizontal line K. In this way, this machine will no longer be able to receive the weak stations CE or the atmospheric noise H. Therefore, when tuning between AB, BD, or DF, the noise received must be very small, or even completely absent. Therefore, this selectivity control can be regarded as a kind of inter-station noise suppression. However, we must remember that in order to weaken the selectivity, the volume of all stations must also be reduced accordingly. But this reduction in volume can be adjusted by improving the volume control.

Because the level of atmospheric noise will vary depending on the area and reception conditions, this inter-station noise suppression is made into a variable control, so that its selectivity is also reduced until the atmospheric noise is no longer received at that time. However, we must still remember that after the radio's selectivity is weakened, it cannot tune in the sounds of weaker stations, and the sounds of the stations that can be received must be accompanied by the same proportion of atmospheric noise. It is useless to reduce the overall volume. (To be continued)

Achievements of Marconi Wireless Telegraph Company in the Past Year

— Dan

1932 was the most progressive and active year for the Marconi Company. We only need to examine the status of the company's important parts to know how important the research on radio and the increase and development of the application of radio in land, sea, and air have been in the past year. 1. Radio Research and its General Development Status

Among the entire radio industry, the most outstanding in 1932 and full of possibilities for realization in the future is the application of [microwaves] with wavelengths shorter than one meter, which Marconi declared and is theoretically considered to be able to reach very far distances.

Marconi and his assistants have sacrificed a lot of time to study the application of these extremely short waves. They have conducted experimental transmissions over a distance of more than 168 kilometers between Rogodi in the vicinity of Rome and Fagliari, Sardinia. As a result, it is clear that these extremely short sound waves can avoid the various obstacles caused by the curvature of the Earth's surface.

Secondly, what attracted the attention of experts and the general public around the world was the Marconi engineers' research on wireless television over the past two years. Last August, the Marconi Company in Chamesford used wireless radio to transmit television news between Britain and St. Peter's College in York, printing news messages on a moving tape for broadcasting at a speed of 120 words per minute. Receivers could easily read it on a glass plate on a teletype machine.

Based on the above, it can be seen that the Marconi Company has completed its particularly reliable wireless television work. It is said that they will continue to develop this issue to be used commercially and for entertainment, i.e., used in radio broadcasting, homes, open-air stages, and theaters.

In general, radio science has made great progress in recent years. That is, the number and power of radio stations have increased, and the methods of managing radio waves have become increasingly thorough. In terms of reception, the sound selection methods of radios have also greatly improved. Therefore, there are renewed requirements for calculators, such as electromagnetic field strength calculators needed to improve practicality, and accurate and portable signal strength indicators. The Marconi Company has also successfully researched and achieved them. They have been very effective in various electromagnetic calculations and have also created many machines that are extremely useful for the development of power stations in the future.

The new short-wave reflector antenna has been tested at the Summerton radio station and has achieved very good results. This new type of antenna is easy to set up, occupies less space than the ordinary antenna used by the Balkoni radio station, and can obtain the same concentration of radio waves.

In terms of sound reception, sensitive commercial radios have been well developed and have been adopted by the Badak Post Office. These advanced short-wave radios used to receive reflected radio waves have been improved, the most important point being the invention of echo prevention.

What is Expected of Broadcasting Stations

— Zhenzhi

I think radio broadcasting stations have at least two missions: one is to transmit news, and the other is to promote culture. For the former, there is nothing more to improve besides making the news timely and accurate. However, for the latter, there are many points for improvement. I will briefly mention one or two points based on my personal views for selection.

First, China has been promoting Mandarin education for more than ten years, but there have been no significant achievements so far. The reason is nothing more than listening and speaking less. The role of the Mandarin phonetic symbols is only to enable people to pronounce accurately, but not to enable people to speak fluently. Therefore, although every elementary school teacher can understand the pronunciation of each word, the result is that they still cannot speak fluent Mandarin. If what the teachers speak is not fluent, then what the students learn is of course conceivable. If this continues, I don't know when Mandarin will be popularized throughout the country. I think radio is a powerful tool for promoting Mandarin education. Every broadcasting station should take on the responsibility of popularizing Mandarin. In addition to academic lectures and other programs, all other programs such as current affairs reports, advertisements, and introductions to each program must be broadcast in Mandarin. It would be even better if more Mandarin programs could be set up specifically.

Second, in order to promote the education of the common people, I hope that major broadcasting stations will reduce programs of low taste as much as possible and increase various popular lecture programs, and send the daily lecture topics to various newspapers for collection and disclosure, so that listeners can freely choose the topics they are concerned about and interested in.

Third, Japan, Europe, and the United States have recently popularized a kind of radio literature, which incorporates various meaningful novels, stories, science, etc. into interesting dialogues, similar to China's [next-door drama]. We can imitate this method, or entrust someone to translate it, or hire someone to create it. I think that as long as each broadcasting station expresses a need, the manuscripts will definitely come in droves. However, this kind of broadcasting talent needs special training. If the people from the performing arts troupes are still called in to broadcast, the result will definitely be like the transformation of vernacular drama into civilization drama.

Radio Common Sense (2)

— Wei

(2) What is a Radio Wave?

Since radio does not rely on electric wires for transmission, then what exactly is it? I can offer an analogy here. Please try throwing a stone into a pond and observe what happens. The moment the stone hits the water, the surface is disturbed, and waves arise, spreading outwards in circles. Gradually, the wavefronts become lower and lower, until everything is completely calm again. If a floating piece of wood is placed within the area where the waves are occurring, the wood will be agitated and will move up and down. Consider that the stone and the wood are not connected by any rope. The relationship between them is entirely dependent on the waves for transmission. Radio is the same, relying on radio waves for transmission. However, water waves are visible, while radio waves are invisible. The generation of water waves originates from the movement of the stone, while the generation of radio waves originates from the movement of electricity. The medium for transmitting water waves is water, while the medium for transmitting radio waves is the invisible [Ether] (Ether). What the ether is remains unclear to this day, but scholars, for the sake of convenient explanation, assume that this ether permeates the universe, just as the atmosphere permeates the Earth.

If we carefully observe the occurrence of water waves, we see that they have crests and troughs. One crest and one trough together make up one cycle. Similarly, one crest and one trough of a radio wave are also called one cycle (Cycle). The length of a water wave cycle is called the wavelength (WaveLength). Radio waves are also the same. The frequency of water waves depends on the manner in which the stone is thrown, and the frequency of radio waves also depends on the speed of electrical oscillation. Denser water waves have shorter wavelengths, while sparser waves have longer wavelengths. Faster electrical oscillation generates shorter wavelengths, while slower oscillation generates longer wavelengths. However, because the speed of radio wave propagation is the same as that of light, approximately 300,000,000 meters per second (i.e., 300,000 kilometers), knowing the number of cycles per second (i.e., frequency) allows one to determine the wavelength. This is because one only needs to divide the distance of 300,000,000 meters by the frequency. (In the diagram above, ABCDE represents one cycle. From A to E, or from B to F, and H to K, all represent wavelengths.)

Each radio station emits radio waves with different wavelengths, which means their frequencies are different. Radio waves are generally classified into the following types. Most of the waves used by broadcasting stations nowadays are medium waves, ranging from 200 meters to 3000 meters. Next, we will discuss what electric current is, how radio waves are emitted, and how radio waves can be received.

Rich general knowledge. This kind of knowledge can be found in books and textbooks in childhood. For intellectuals, it can be found in news magazines, which is not difficult. However, farmers in the interior who have not received education and laborers who work hard all day do not have this time. Second, for entertainment, the hard-working masses are busy all day long. If there is no entertainment to comfort them, they will lose the joy of life. Although people in the metropolis have many leisure activities such as movies and dramas, it is not a concern. However, farmers and workers in the countryside cannot do without radio. Third, for reporting. The Chinese people have always been less informed about national affairs. They regard the rise and fall of the country as not their concern. However, it is not that they really do not want to hear about it, but that there is no way to know. Now, if radio is used to report to the public at all times, so that the people can understand the general situation at home and abroad and develop their ability to participate in politics, then the benefits to the future of the country will be immeasurable.

In addition, radio weather forecasts can enable farmers and fishermen to prepare for a rainy day. Academic lectures can provide scholars and literati with more opportunities to benefit. Radio exercises and the broadcast of sports news also convey the purpose of physical training, and the storytelling of literature and stories also has the effect of moral education. Morality, intellect, and physical education are all beneficial, which is what we should not ignore.

Radio is so important to the public. Therefore, all European and American countries are striving to use it. Our eastern neighbor Japan is even more eager to catch up, with more than a dozen large radio stations broadcasting various programs every morning and evening. Since the Manchurian Incident, there has been no day without political speeches to cover up its aggressive ambitions, and to completely unify the thoughts of the people of the whole country under the will of the warlords. This method of unifying national will is most convenient with radio.

In short, the benefits of radio are not only in communication, but also in being a great tool for public education. It is not only a tool for education, but also can achieve the effect of unifying national opinion. Now China has such a vast territory, such a low level of education, and such scattered thoughts of the people. This is the time to use radio. I hope the people of the country will pay attention to it.

Radio Receivers in Nature

— Qi

The ability of certain animals to emit light, electricity, and odors are relatively common and easily detectable phenomena. There is also a less noticeable phenomenon, which is the emission of radio waves by certain animals.

We know that homing pigeons, when released from a distance, can fly back to their original location on their own. Bats have very weak eyesight, but they can prey on small insects at night. Furthermore, zoologists tell us that lemmings in the high mountains of Norway often leave their nests in groups and make long journeys when the cold season comes, and often proceed in straight lines towards a certain destination, just like old horses that know the way.

These mysterious phenomena have not been able to obtain accurate and satisfactory explanations. According to the French radio expert Lacassagne, certain animals do have the ability to emit and receive radio waves. The antennae of insects are just like the cat's whisker in a crystal radio, with the function of picking up electromagnetic waves. Moreover, most animals have a special organ in their inner ear, consisting of three semi-circular canals. It is said that this organ has the ability to indicate direction. When animals lose it, they are at a loss for direction, as if they are in a fog. Most interestingly, the above-mentioned canals contain a liquid substance that is extremely sensitive to magnetic force. We know that radio broadcasters can generate variable magnetic fields around them, so we can even say that the semi-circular canals are radio receivers capable of sensing this kind of magnetic force change!

According to this theory, the aforementioned mysterious phenomena can be explained as follows:

(1) When a homing pigeon flies up, it generates electricity by friction between its body and the air, and then rises or falls, forming a variable capacitor between its body and the ground. When it reaches a certain balance, it flies horizontally. This natural capacitor is the link between the two locations.

(2) Bats can prey on insects at night by using certain electromagnetic waves emitted by the latter as targets.

(3) Lemmings can move towards a distant destination by using the radio waves emitted by fish there as targets.

Whether this hypothesis is reliable remains to be studied jointly by radio experts and biologists, or a practical answer can be obtained. I will record it here temporarily, just for the sake of providing topics for conversation after dinner.

All Kinds of Antennas

— Jin Yunqiao

(1) The Role of Antennas in Radio Receivers

The name antenna specifically refers to the overhead wire erected outdoors. With the progress of radio technology today, indoor antennas can be used near power stations or in radios with high-frequency amplification. (For radios using indoor antennas, the high-frequency amplification part should be stronger than those using outdoor antennas, and the number of stages must be increased appropriately, otherwise it will be difficult to obtain satisfactory results.) Or even those who abandon the indoor ones are also exempt from using them.

The Western word for antenna is Antenna, which translates to insect antennae. Its importance to radio receivers is evident. The music and language of the broadcasting station, after the work of the microphone and vacuum tubes, are released by the antenna in the form of high-frequency radio waves, and then transmitted through the ether in the air, reaching everywhere. The antenna of the receiving station absorbs these radio waves and transmits them into the radio. We only need to increase or decrease the inductance of the induction coil and the capacitance of the capacitor in the radio, adjust it to the same point as the wavelength of the broadcasting station, so that resonance occurs, and then through the detector, the high-frequency current is changed to low-frequency, and then into the earphones or amplifier, and it becomes sound waves. Since the antenna is composed of a wire of considerable length, it has electrical storage and inductance. Its interaction with the ground wire is like a large capacitor, with the air in the middle insulating it. According to the definition of capacitance, the closer the distance between two metal plates, the greater the capacitance, and the smaller the area, the smaller the capacitance, otherwise the opposite is true. Therefore, the higher the antenna, the smaller the capacitance, but the induced voltage is strengthened. The longer the antenna, the greater the capacitance. The adjustment and reception of radio waves mostly depends on the action of capacitance and inductance. The sensitivity of the radio depends on this. (To be continued)

Radio in the Countryside

Italian Prime Minister Mussolini recently opened a very important agricultural exhibition, the main purpose of which was to persuade farmers to install radios in their farms. He believes that with a radio nearby, farmers are like being in the city, and can use it to discuss the prices of their products with people in the city, and can also know how to improve the tools they use. He regards the radio as a kind of agricultural tool.

Reader Research

An Economical AC Three-Tube Receiver

— Ren Xinyu

In the current trend of radio receivers leaning towards AC power, I think many amateur researchers would like to make an AC receiver to play with. Because AC receivers are not only easy to manage and have low running costs, but also have better effectiveness; however, the device is more complicated and the value is slightly more expensive, so many researchers shy away from it. I recently made a three-tube receiver, although it only has one stage of detection and one stage of low-frequency amplification, the volume is very large, the selectivity is also good, and the value is very low. It is worth trying for general economic comrades. Now I will write down my experience for the reference of others. Vacuum tubes use two 227s and one 210A.

The circuit and parts are shown in the attached diagram.

The tuning coil uses a one-inch inner diameter spider web board, and is wound with 24-gauge wire for 63 turns, with one tap every nine turns. The regenerative coil is wound with the same gauge wire for 45 turns, and is installed on a push-pull frame for advancement and retreat.

The core of the power transformer is a one-inch square cross-sectional area. The primary uses 30-gauge wire for 1800 turns; to supply the filament current for two 227s, use two 16-gauge wires in parallel for 23 turns, with a center tap at 11 and a half turns; to supply 201, use 24-gauge wire for 45 turns, also with a center tap; the high-voltage coil uses 38-gauge wire for 1600 turns; wax paper must be used to separate each layer, and several layers of wax paper must be wound between the primary and each secondary. Choke coils can be made by connecting two old low-frequency square-frame secondaries in series, or use 30H products.

After the components are installed, if you feel that the selectivity is not satisfactory, you can reduce the capacity of the capacitor in the antenna circuit a little. Although the sound quality is reduced, the selectivity is increased a lot. The incoming wire of the power supply and the wiring of the filament machine must use stranded wire, otherwise there may be very large AC noise; it is better to put a purple copper soft sleeve on the outside and ground it, so that the AC noise is further reduced. The iron core of the power supply part must also be grounded to avoid mutual induction. After I listened to this radio for several days, I felt that the volume on the long wavelength side was very light, and I tried various methods to improve it, but they were all ineffective. Later, I added a coil to the antenna and ground wire, using a three-inch diameter for 50 turns, with one tap every five turns, one end connected to the antenna and one end connected to the ground wire. When connected in this way, not only the long wave aspect was much louder, but also the short aspect was much louder. However, after a few days, I felt that the sound quality was not good, especially the female voice was easily distorted. I accidentally thought of the importance of the bypass capacitor, so I added a 1MF capacitor between B+Det and B丨, and the sound quality was indeed improved a lot. I also added a high-frequency choke coil at X in the attached diagram. The manufacturing method is as follows: Prepare two bakelite boards, and file them into a circle, one inch in diameter, and then cut the bamboo sleeve of the brush, about three or four minutes in diameter, into three minutes long, clamp it in the middle of the two small round plates, and tighten it with screws, like the wheel of a rickshaw, and then use 38-gauge wire to wind about 1700 turns on the bamboo tube. Use another capacitor, one end connected to the choke coil and one end connected to the ground wire. In this way, I feel that the volume and selectivity have increased a bit. Now my improvement of this radio can be considered complete, and I will tell you more about it in the future. The materials for this radio, except for the vacuum tubes and copper wire, can all be bought from domestic goods, and wireless comrades may wish to try it.
